F.F. Goryayev, A.M. Urnov and L.A. Vainshtein

February 15, 2014

Atomic data calculations by Z-expansion method for doubly ex-

cited states 2lnl′ and 1s2lnl′ of highly charged ions with Z = 6
I. Transitions from the states with n = 2, 3.

−

29.

Abstract

The wavelengths and radiative transition probabilities for transitions
2lnl′ − 1snl′′, 2lnl′ − 1s2l′′, 1s2lnl′ − 1s2nl′′, 1s2lnl′ − 1s2
2l′′, and the
autoionization decay probabilities for doubly excited states 2lnl′, 1s2lnl′
were calculated in ions with atomic numbers Z = 6 − 29 for n = 2 − 10,
l′
= 0 − 3. The calculations were carried out by means of the MZ code
based on the Z-expansion method. Relativistic corrections were taken into
account within the framework of the Breit operator. The main diﬀerence
with previous calculations by MZ code consists in accounting for the ﬁrst
order corrections in powers of 1/Z, corresponding to the screening eﬀects,
in calculations of autoionization rates. New data for comparatively large
rates are about 20-50% less as compared to previous ones and are in a
agreement within 10% with the results of calculations made by the meth-
ods based on multi-conﬁguration wave functions with non-relativistic and
relativistic orbitals. Some reﬁnements and corrections concerning the en-
ergies and radiative transition probabilities were also introduced in the
MZ code. In this paper the main formulas used in a modiﬁed MZ-code
and the data needed for description of dielectronic satellites with n = 2, 3
are given; the data for higher n will be presented in the following publi-
cations.

1 Introduction

Dielectronic satellite (DS) spectra in the vicinity of the resonance lines of [H]
and [He] ions provide the important information on electron temperature, den-
sity, ionization state and other characteristics of hot plasmas and are widely
used in spectroscopic diagnostics. For unambiguous analysis and modeling of
DS spectra one usually needs to have a large amount of atomic data: wave-
lengths, radiative transition probabilities and autoionization rates, calculated
with high accuracy. The approach of expansion over 1/Z (Z is the nuclear

1

charge), called also ”Z-expansion” method, is an eﬀective one for determina-
tion of atomic characteristics for highly charged ions. MZ code based on this
approach was developed for the calculations of wavelengths and transition prob-
abilities. The input information (coeﬃcients of the Z-expansion) can be used for
an entire isoelectronic sequence and total calculation time on the modern PC is
less than 1 min. However the coeﬃcients of the Z-expansion must be calculated
separately.

The outline of Z-expansion method and the calculations of corresponding
data for DS emitted by [He] and [Li] ions are given in the [1, 2, 3, 4, 5] and
by [Be] through [Ne] ions in the papers [6, 7]. The description of the MZ code
and corresponding formulas are given in the monograph [8]. The systematic
calculations of atomic data for doubly excited states 2lnl′ and 1s2lnl′ of ions
33 by this code have been performed and published in the late
with Z = 6
seventies for n = 2 [4] and n = 3 [9].

−

The comparison of the wavelengths calculated by Z-expansion method with
the experimental data obtained from the tokamak and EBIT K-spectra of [Li]
argon ions [10, 11] has shown that this approach provides better ﬁt to the mea-
sured values than the calculations, employing the MCHF (multi-conﬁguration
Hartree-Fock) [12] or MCDF (Dirac-Fock) method [13, 14]. The radiative prob-
abilities obtained up to the second term over 1/Z have been found in agreement
with the calculations of [12, 13, 14] within 10%, while the autoionization rates,
obtained in the ﬁrst nonvanishing order, diﬀered up to a factor of 2.

The comparison of the satellite lines of [H] and [He] spectra calculated by

the MZ and AUTOLSJ methods for Fe, Ca and S ions is given in [15].

In this work the calculations have been carried out by means of a modi-
ﬁed version of MZ code, completed with some corrections and reﬁnements. In
particular, the second order corrections to the autoionization radial integrals,
corresponding to the screening eﬀects, as well as the contribution of cascade
transitions (3-2) to the intensity of DS have been included. The wavelengths
1s2l′′,
and radiative transition probabilities for transitions 2lnl′
1s2lnl′
1s22l′′ and the autoionization decay probabilities for
doubly excited states 2lnl′, 1s2lnl′ have been calculated in ions with atomic
10, l′ = 0
numbers Z = 6
3. The present paper contains
the main formulas used in a modiﬁed MZ-code and the data for dielectronic
satellites with n = 2, 3; the data for higher n will be given in the following
publications.

electrons and the nuclear charge are denoted through N and Z, respectively.

2 Method of calculation

2.1 Energies

Z-expansion method is based on the perturbation theory expansion over 1/Z
(Z is the nuclear charge), in other words, on the hydrogen-like basis. The
relativistic corrections are included in the framework of the Breit Hamiltonian.
The energy matrix E for a given Layzer complex (states with given J, parity
and set of principal quantum numbers of electrons) can be presented in the form

′

′

′
E(aJ, a

L

) + ES + ∆Exδ(a, a

J) = [EN + ER]δ(SL, S

(4)
Here the matrices EN , ER and ES correspond to the nonrelativistic energy, spin
independent part and spin dependent part of the Breit operator, respectively.
The term ∆Ex is introduced for additional semi-empirical correction. The ma-
trix EN includes the terms up to the second order and the matrices ER and ES
contain the zero and ﬁrst orders (over electrostatic interaction of electrons):
EN = Z 2E0δ (a, a′) + ZE1 + E2

The terms containing ρ0, ǫ0 and ρ1, ǫ1 give the contributions of the zero and
ﬁrst orders from one-particle terms of the Breit operator. The terms including
ρ′, ǫ′ and ǫ′′ correspond to the zero order contributions from two-particle terms.

probability over J0lj to obtain a simpler formula suﬃcient in most practical

3 EXPLANATION OF TABLES

In the Tables Ia, IIa, Ib, IIb the results of calculations are given for atomic
data connected with the transitions from doubly excited states of He-like (I,IIa)
and Li-like (I,IIb) ions with Z=6-29. Data for resonance lines of [H] and [He]
ions as well as for intercombination, magneto-quadrupole and forbidden lines of
[He] ion are also included. The notations as well as the format of these data
are similar to those used in the papers [4], [9]. The set of quantum numbers
describing the initial state is denoted through γ=(aSLJ).

The Tables Ia, IIa, Ib, IIb contain for each transition γ

γ′ the following

→

data:

∆E is transition energy in keV,
λ - wavelength in Angstroms,
A = A(γ, γ′) - probability of radiative decay, Eq.(15), in units 1013 s−1,
Γ(γ) - probability of autoionization, Eq.(17), in units 1013 s−1,
K - branching ratio, Eq.(22),
Qd - satellite intensity factor, Eq.(21-23), in units 1013 s−1.
To avoid a confusion, it is worth to give here the correspondence with the
notations used in some papers quoted above: A = Ar, Γ = Aa, Qd = g0F2. Here
g0 is the statistical weight of the initial state from which DS is excited (1s or
1s2).

In the Tables these data are denoted as follows.
∆E = E , λ = WL, Γ = G.
The set of quantum numbers a (electronic conﬁguration and intermediate
quantum numbers specifying the coupling scheme for angular momenta) is de-
noted through the capital letters:

I. He-like ions

Y=1s C=2s2p A’=2p3d
R=2p E=2s2s B’=2p3s
R’=3p F=2p2p C’=2s3p
P=1s2p F’=2p3p
S=1s2s G’=2s3d
S’=1s3s E’=2s3s
P’=1s3p D’=1s3d

In the Tables below the numbers following the letters mean the statistical
weights (2S+1) (2L+1) (2J+1). For example: R234-Y212 stands for 2p2P3/2-
1s2S1/2 and A’353-D’155 means 2p3d3D1-1s3d1D2.

In conclusion we would like to note that the atomic data presented in Ta-
bles Ia, IIa and Ib, IIb could be provided in another formats (e.g. convinient
for Matlab package) due to request by the adress urnov@sci.lebedev.ru or
vainsh@sci.lebedev.ru.

A.2 Angular parts of transition matrix elements
